## Domain Knowledge
**Domain**: nonlinear dynamics / classical mechanics
**Analysis**: This is a nonlinear harmonic oscillator where acceleration (dv_dt) depends on position, velocity, and possibly time through nonlinear restoring forces, nonlinear damping, and potential external driving. The task seeks the equation of motion in the form dv_dt = f(x, v, t).

**Common formula structures** (built-in generic + LLM domain-specific):
- Arrhenius equation: k = c0 * exp(c1 / T) (chemical reaction rate dependence on temperature)
- Coulomb's / Newton's inverse-square law: F = c0 / r**2 (gravitational or electrostatic force)
- Stefan-Boltzmann law: P = c0 * T**4 (blackbody radiation power vs temperature)
- Beer-Lambert law: I = c0 * exp(c1 * x) (light intensity attenuation through a medium)
- Michaelis-Menten kinetics: v = c0 * S / (S + c1) (enzyme-catalyzed reaction saturation)
- Hill equation: y = c0 * x**c1 / (x**c1 + c2) (cooperative binding, sigmoidal dose-response)
- Kepler's third law: T**2 = c0 * a**3 (orbital period vs semi-major axis)
- Newton's law of cooling: T = c0 + c1 * exp(c2 * t) (exponential thermal relaxation)
- Clausius-Clapeyron relation: log(P) = c0 + c1 / T (vapor pressure vs temperature)
- Langmuir adsorption isotherm: theta = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) (surface adsorption equilibrium)
- Freundlich isotherm: q = c0 * C**c1 (empirical adsorption on heterogeneous surface)
- Stokes' drag: F = c0 * r * v (viscous drag force on a sphere in fluid)
- Logistic growth: N = c0 / (1 + c1 * exp(c2 * t)) (population dynamics with carrying capacity)
- Planck-Wien approximation: I = c0 * f**3 * exp(c1 * f / T) (thermal radiation spectrum)
- Linear harmonic oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x (simple restoring force)
- Damped harmonic oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v (linear restoring + linear damping)
- Duffing oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 (cubic nonlinear restoring force)
- Damped Duffing oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * v (cubic restoring + damping)
- Driven Duffing oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * v + c3 * cos(c4 * t) (forced nonlinear oscillator)
- Van der Pol oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v * (1 + c2 * x**2) (nonlinear damping)
- Quintic nonlinear oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * x**5 (higher-order restoring force)
- Pendulum-like: dv_dt = c0 * sin(c1 * x) (sinusoidal restoring force)
- Damped pendulum: dv_dt = c0 * sin(c1 * x) + c2 * v (sinusoidal restoring + damping)
- Quadratic nonlinearity: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**2 (asymmetric restoring force)
- Nonlinear damping with cubic: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v + c2 * v**3 (velocity-dependent nonlinear friction)
- Rayleigh oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v + c2 * v**3 + c3 * x**3 (combined nonlinearities)
- Parametric oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x * cos(c1 * t) + c2 * v (time-modulated stiffness)
- Coulomb + viscous damping: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v + c2 * v * x**2 (mixed nonlinear terms)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Odd-symmetry restoring force → odd powers of x only (x, x³, x⁵) indicating symmetric potential well
- Nonlinear damping → velocity terms multiplied by position powers (v·x², v·x⁴) indicating amplitude-dependent energy dissipation
- Self-excited oscillation → negative linear damping + positive nonlinear damping (c0*v + c1*v³ with opposite signs)
- Periodic driving → trigonometric functions of time cos(c·t) or sin(c·t) indicating external forcing
- Softening/hardening spring → sign of cubic coefficient x³ determines whether resonance frequency decreases/increases with amplitude
- Broken symmetry → even powers of x (x²) indicating asymmetric potential well
- Parametric excitation → product of x with periodic time function x·cos(c·t) indicating time-varying stiffness
- Conservative system → acceleration depends only on x with no v or t dependence, implying energy conservation

GT: -omega0**c0*(gamma*Abs(v)**c1 + c2)*x - omega0**c3*x**c4
Candidate formulas: 50

I need to determine if any candidate formula can match the GT:

**GT:** `-1.68187*x**3 - 1.68187*x*(0.04381*|v|^(1/3) + 1)`

Expanding: `-1.68187*x - 1.68187*0.04381*|v|^(1/3)*x - 1.68187*x**3`

So GT = `-1.68187*x - 0.073697*|v|^(1/3)*x - 1.68187*x**3`

The key feature is the `|v|^(1/3)` term. This is `Abs(v)^(1/3)`, which is a cube root of the absolute value. Since we're in a physics oscillator context where v can be negative, `|v|^(1/3)` is NOT the same as `v^(1/3)` (which would be odd for real cube roots but complex for negative values in many conventions).

The GT has three terms:
1. A term proportional to `x`
2. A term proportional to `|v|^(1/3) * x`
3. A term proportional to `x^3`

None of the candidates contain `|v|^(1/3)` or `Abs(v)` terms. So I need to check if any candidate's functional forms can approximate or exactly match `|v|^(1/3)`.

Let me look at what functional forms of v appear in candidates:
- `v**2*x`, `v**4*x` — polynomial in v²
- `v**2*x/(c + v**2)` — rational in v²
- `log(c*v**2 + 1)` — logarithmic in v²
- `exp(c*v**2)` — exponential in v²
- `cos(c*v)` — trigonometric in v

The GT requires `|v|^(1/3)*x`. This is a non-analytic function at v=0 (it has a cusp). 

- Polynomials in v² are smooth and even in v, but can't produce `|v|^(1/3)`.
- `v²/(c + v²)` approaches 0 as v→0 and 1 as v→∞, can't match `|v|^(1/3)`.
- `log(c*v² + 1)` behaves like `c*v²` near 0 and `log(v²)` for large v — not `|v|^(1/3)`.
- `exp(c*v²)` — exponential, not a match.
- `cos(c*v)` — even in v, analytic, can't match the cusp behavior.

No combination of these smooth/analytic functions can exactly equal `|v|^(1/3)`, which has a non-analytic cusp at v=0 and grows as a fractional power.

Even combining multiple terms (like rational functions, logs, exponentials), none can produce the exact `|v|^(1/3)` behavior. The question asks for **mathematical equivalence**, not approximation.

Since none of the candidates contain any fractional power of |v| or v, and the GT fundamentally requires `|v|^(1/3)`, no candidate can be made mathematically equivalent to the GT.

Let me double-check: could the `|v|^(1/3)` term be absorbed if its coefficient γ could be set to 0? Looking at the GT: γ = 0.04381 is a **fixed** GT constant, not a free parameter. The GT is fixed. So the `|v|^(1/3)` term is definitely present in the GT and cannot be eliminated.

Therefore, no candidate can exactly match the GT.

[NO MATCH]

$$f(x,v) = -1.68187 x^3 - 1.68187 x (0.04381 |v|^{1/3} + 1)$$

Expanding:
$$f(x,v) = -1.68187 x - 0.07369 |v|^{1/3} x - 1.68187 x^3$$

The key basis functions in the GT are:
1. $x$ (linear term)
2. $|v|^{1/3} \cdot x$ (cube root of |v| times x)
3. $x^3$ (cubic term)

The critical feature is $|v|^{1/3} \cdot x$ — this is a fractional power of $|v|$. Let me check which candidates can reproduce this.

**Key observation:** None of the candidates contain $|v|^{1/3}$ explicitly. The candidates use:
- $v^2 \cdot x$ terms (polynomial in $v$)
- $v^2/(c + v^2)$ rational functions of $v^2$
- $\log(c \cdot v^2 + 1)$ 
- $\exp(c \cdot v^2)$
- $\cos(c \cdot v)$
- Various polynomial terms in $x$

**Can any of these reproduce $|v|^{1/3}$?**

- **Polynomials in $v^2$**: These are smooth even functions. $|v|^{1/3}$ has a cusp at $v=0$ and grows as a fractional power — cannot be matched by any finite polynomial.

- **$v^2/(c + v^2)$**: This is a bounded rational function approaching 1 as $|v| \to \infty$. $|v|^{1/3}$ is unbounded. Cannot match.

- **$\log(c \cdot v^2 + 1)$**: This grows as $\log(v^2)$ for large $|v|$, not as $|v|^{1/3}$. These are fundamentally different functions — logarithmic vs. power law growth. They are NOT equivalent for all $v$.

- **$\exp(c \cdot v^2)$**: For $c \neq 0$, this either grows super-exponentially or decays. Cannot match $|v|^{1/3}$.

- **$\cos(c \cdot v)$**: Bounded and periodic. Cannot match.

- **Combinations**: Even combining $v^2 x$, $v^2 x/(c+v^2)$, $\log(cv^2+1) x$, etc., these are all smooth functions of $v$ (or have logarithmic singularity structure), while $|v|^{1/3}$ has a specific fractional power behavior. By linear independence of these function classes, no finite combination can exactly equal $|v|^{1/3}$ for all $v$.

Since **every** candidate lacks the $|v|^{1/3}$ basis function and cannot reproduce it through any combination of their available terms, **none** of the candidates can exactly match the GT.

Let me verify there's no way to set the coefficient of the $|v|^{1/3}$ term to zero: The GT has $\gamma = 0.04381$ which is fixed and nonzero. The GT constants are FIXED, so we cannot eliminate this term.

Therefore, every candidate is a [NO MATCH].
